The Sutra in Prayer: Dimensions, Placement, and Repelling Passersby
Expansion on sutra rules from a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutra's dimensions and method of placement, and apply the rule for repelling passersby.

Core Idea
A sutra must be a physical object of about a cubit length and finger thickness, fixed firmly, and the pray-er must repel anyone who crosses.

The sutra (screen) is a sunnah mu'akkadah for the one praying, whether alone or leading. This lesson explores its recommended dimensions, how it should be placed, and what to do if someone tries to pass in front of you. We will also examine a key internal Hanafi difference: whether drawing a line suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that using a sutra is a sunnah (recommended) act for the one praying. It is not wajib or fard, but strongly encouraged.
The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil for dimensions
The commentator cites the hadith of ‘Ā’isha: the Prophet compared the sutra to the back of a camel saddle (مثل مؤخرة الرحل). From this, scholars derived the recommended length of about a cubit.
This hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear, so it suffices for a sunnah ruling.
3
Analyse the method of placement
The sutra should be fixed (gharz) into the ground, not merely placed on the ground. The pray-er should stand close to it, aligning it with one of his temples.
The word 'gharz' implies inserting firmly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on drawing a line
Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani said a line drawn on the ground is sufficient if no object is available. The majority of Hanafis disagree, holding that a physical sutra is required, and a line does not suffice.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view.
5
Apply the rule for repelling passersby
If someone tries to pass in front of the one praying, he should repel (yadra'u) the passerby as much as he can. This is based on an authentic hadith in Bukhari and Muslim.
The permission to repel applies whether or not a sutra is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاذى الأعضاء الأعضاء لو كان على دكان، ويَغْرِزُ أمامَهُ في الصحراء سترة بقدرِ ذراع، وغلظ أصبع ولهذا قال : وحاذى الأعضاء الأعضاء لو كان على دكان)، أخذا بالرواية الثانية. ويَغْرِزُ أمامه في الصحراء سترة بقدر ذراع" ، وغِلَظ أُصبع " كلها كما قاله بعضُهم أو أكثرها كما قاله آخرون، كما في الكرماني، وفيه إشعار بأنه لو حاذى أقلها أو نصفها لم يكره). [١] قوله : بالرواية الثانية ؛ قال في الإسفرائيني : «ذكروا الاختلاف في موضع السجود، وذكروا مسألة الدكان من غير بيان خلاف، فحقق الشارح بأنَّ هذه المسألة إنما تبتني على القول الثاني، لكن لا يخفى أنّ المسجد الصغير يستوي فيه الدكان وغيره. فينبغي أن يخص حكمه المبين بغير المسجد الصغير، ففي عبارة المتن قصور، ويمكن أن يقال : البحث عن الدكان ليس مبنياً على أنّ ما تحت الدكان، بل هو موضعُ السجود أو لا؟ بل مبني على أنّ الكونَ (۲) على الدكّان هل هو بمنزلة الحائل أم لا»(3). [٢] قوله : ويغرز ؛ بكسر الراء المهملة ، من الغَرز بفتح الغين المعجمة ؛ أي يدخلُ رأس السترة في الأرض على الاستقامة، وضميره يرجعُ إلى المصلى، وهو مستحب له، منفرداً كان أو إماماً، وسترته سترة للمقتدي. [٣]قوله : بقدر ذراع ؛ أي طولاً يؤخذ ذلك من حديث عائشة رضي الله عنها : سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن سترة المصلي فقال: «مثل مؤخرة الرحل، أخرجه مسلم وغيره، وهو بضم الميم وسكون الهمزة وكسر الخاء المعجمة : العود الذي يكون في آخر رحل البعير، ومقداره يكون غالباً ذراعاً. [٤]قوله : وغلظ أصبع ؛ أي يكون غلظه وعرضه بقدر غلظ الأصبع لتبدو بقربه على أحد حاجبيه، ولا توضع، ولا يُخَطِّ، ويدرأه) للناظر، لما روى «أنه صلى إلى عنزة ) ، أخرجه البخاري وغيرُه ، ومقداره طول ذراع وغلظ الأصبع. [١] قوله : بقربه ؛ متعلّق بالغرز، وذلك لحديث: «إذا صلى أحدكم إلى سترة فليدن منها (۲) ، أخرجه أبو داود وابن حبان والطبراني وغيرهم. (۲) قوله : على أحد حاجبيه ؛ أي محاذياً لحاجبه الأيمن أو الأيسر، هو المنقول عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، أخرجه أبو داود والطبراني. (۳) قوله : ولا توضع؛ أي لا تلقى السترة على الأرض بل تغرز ؛ لأن المقصود لا يحصل به، وكذا لا يحصلُ بالخط في الأرض، وهذا هو قول أكثر أصحابنا. وروى عن أبي يوسف و محمد الله بكفاية الوضع إذا لم يكن الغرز والخط إذا لم يجد سترة كالمحراب ؛ لحديث: «فإن لم يكن عصاً فليخط خطا(۳)، أخرجه أبو داود وابن ماجة، وفي سنده ضعف غير مانع ؛ لجواز العمل به في الفضائل ، قال ابن الهمام ) : «السنة أولى بالاتباع». [٤]قوله : ويدرأه ؛ من الدرء بالفتح بمعنى الدفع أي يدفع المصلّي المار بين يديه إذا لم يكن بين يديه سترة أو كانت ومرّ بينه وبين السترة ؛ لقوله : «إذا كان أحدكم يُصلّي فلا يدع أحداً يمر بين يديه، وليدراً ما استطاع» ()، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم.
And [the pray-er] should align the limbs when on a platform, and he should fix in front of him in an open plain a sutra of about a cubit [in height] and a finger's thickness. For this reason he said: 'And align the limbs when on a platform' adopting the second narration. 'And he fixes in front of him in the open plain a sutra of about a cubit' and a finger's thickness. All of it as some said, or most of it as others said, as in al-Kirmāni, and there is an indication that if he aligns less than that or half of it, it is not disliked. [1] His statement: 'by the second narration'; said in al-Isfarā'īnī: 'They mentioned the difference regarding the place of prostration, and they mentioned the issue of the platform without clarifying the difference, so the commentator verified that this issue is based on the second opinion, but it is not hidden that in a small mosque the platform and other than it are equal. So his ruling should be specified for other than a small mosque, so in the expression of the text there is deficiency, and it can be said: The inquiry about the platform is not based on whether what is under the platform is the place of prostration or not? Rather it is based on whether being on the platform is like a barrier or not.' [2] His statement: 'and he fixes'; with kasra on the ra, from gharz (with fatha on ghayn); meaning he inserts the head of the sutra into the ground straight, and its pronoun refers to the pray-er, and it is recommended for him, whether alone or an imam, and his sutra is a sutra for the follower. [3] His statement: 'about a cubit'; meaning length, this is taken from the hadith of 'Ā'isha (may Allah be pleased with her): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about the sutra of the one praying, so he said: 'Like the back of the camel saddle', Muslim and others narrated it. It means with damma on the mim, sukun on the hamza, and kasra on the khā': the stick that is at the back of the camel's saddle, and its measure is generally a cubit. [4] His statement: 'and a finger's thickness'; meaning its thickness and width is about the thickness of a finger, so that it appears with him on one of his temples, and it should not be placed (on the ground), nor should a line be drawn, and he should repel (the passerby) because he prayed facing a spear, narrated by Bukhari and others, and its measure is a cubit in length and a finger's thickness. [1] His statement: 'with him'; related to fixing, and that is due to the hadith: 'When one of you prays towards a sutra let him come close to it', narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani and others. [2] His statement: 'on one of his temples'; meaning aligned with his right or left temple, this is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tabarani. [3] His statement: 'and it should not be placed'; meaning the sutra should not be thrown on the ground but rather fixed; because the purpose is not achieved by that, and similarly it is not achieved by a line on the ground. This is the saying of most of our companions. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with them) the sufficiency of placing if fixing is not possible, and the line if one does not find a sutra like the mihrab; due to the hadith: 'If there is no stick, let him draw a line', narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah, and its chain has weakness not preventing acting upon it in virtues; Ibn al-Humam said: 'The Sunnah is more worthy of following'. [4] His statement: 'and he should repel it'; from al-dar' with fatha meaning to push, i.e., the one praying pushes the passerby in front of him if there is no sutra in front of him or if there is one and someone passes between him and the sutra; because of his saying: 'When one of you prays, let him not allow anyone to pass in front of him, and let him repel as much as he can', narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of the sutra (screen) in prayer, taken from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah. The commentator explains the recommended dimensions of the sutra: the length should be about a cubit (approximately arm's length) based on the hadith comparing it to the back of a saddle, and the thickness should be about a finger's width. The sutra is inserted (gharz) into the ground, not merely placed on it, and the pray-er should stand close to it, aligning it with one of his temples. A line drawn on the ground is not sufficient according to most Hanafi scholars, though a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allows drawing a line if no physical sutra is available, citing a hadith with a weak chain. However, the relied-upon position is that the line is not sufficient, as the sunnah is to use a physical object. The passage also discusses the ruling on a platform (dakkan): if one prays on a platform, he should align his limbs with those of the person behind, based on the second narration regarding the place of prostration. Finally, the pray-er is instructed to repel anyone who tries to pass in front of him, whether or not he has a sutra, based on authentic hadith. All rulings are from the Hanafi school, with internal differences noted.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of the one praying as a screen to prevent passersby from crossing before him.
غرز (gharz): To insert the sutra into the ground firmly, as opposed to merely placing it.
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, approximately the length from the elbow to the fingertips, used as the recommended height of the sutra.
درأ (dara'a): To push or repel, specifically the action of the one praying to prevent a passerby from crossing in front of him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the minimum acceptable sutra if one cannot fix an object into the ground?
A) A line drawn on the ground.
B) A physical object, even if not fixed.
C) Any object, even a small stone, is sufficient.
D) A physical object must be fixed; if not possible, one may pray without a sutra.

Key Takeaway
The sutra is a physical object (cubit length, finger thickness) fixed into the ground; a line is not sufficient; the pray-er must repel passersby.

Sutrah in Prayer: Placement and Repelling Passersby
Commentary on sutrah placement and repelling passersby with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutrah (sunnah muakkadah), identify the condition for its validity (planting vs. placing), and apply the method of repelling a passerby (tasbih for men, clapping for women).

Core Idea
The sutrah is a confirmed sunnah; planting it fulfills the sunnah better than drawing a line.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the detailed rulings on the sutrah (barrier) in prayer and how to repel anyone who tries to pass in front of you. The author begins by describing the proper placement of the sutrah – close to the worshipper and aligned with the eyebrow – and then addresses the controversy regarding whether the sutrah must be planted or can simply be placed or even drawn as a line. The passage also clarifies the permissible methods for repelling a passerby, distinguishing between men and women, and explains the imam's sutrah suffices for the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Using a sutrah in prayer. Determine the hukm level: sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended). The proof is the hadith commanding closeness to the sutrah.
The ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers.
2
Locate the dalil for planting vs. placing
The text cites the Prophet's practice of praying towards a spear (anzah) and the command to be close. The majority of Hanafis require planting (gharz) because placing or drawing a line does not achieve the intended barrier.
The sahih hadith supports planting; the hadith about drawing a line is weak.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow placing or drawing a line if planting is not possible, citing a weak hadith. The Hanafi response is that the weak hadith may be used for virtues, but the stronger practice (planting) is preferred. Tarjih: planting is mufta bihi.
Ibn al-Humam states: 'The sunnah is worthier of being followed.'
4
Determine the method of repelling a passerby
If someone tries to pass in front of the worshipper (and there is no sutrah or the passer goes between the sutrah and the worshipper), the worshiper may repel by saying 'Subhanallah' (tasbih) or by a subtle gesture. Men use tasbih; women clap. Combining both is disliked.
The repelling is permissible (ibaha) but not obligatory.
5
Note the imam's sutrah and omission scenario
The imam's sutrah suffices for the followers, based on the Prophet's practice at Batha' Mecca. If no one passes and the worshipper does not face a road, the sutrah may be omitted without harm.
Leaving the sutrah when needed is disliked, but the prayer remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْقُربِهِ عَلَى أَحَدِ حَاجِبَيْهِ، وَلَا تُوضَعُ، وَلَا يُخَطِّ، وَيَدْرَأُهُ) لِلنَّاظِرِ، لِمَا رُوِيَ «أَنَّهُ صَلَّى إِلَى عَنَزَةٍ» أَخْرَجَهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ وَغَيْرُهُ، وَمِقْدَارُهُ طُولُ ذِرَاعٍ وَغِلَظُ الْأُصْبَعِ. [١] قَوْلُهُ: بِقُرْبِهِ؛ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِالْغَرْزِ، وَذَلِكَ لِحَدِيثِ: «إِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى سُتْرَةٍ فَلْيَدْنُ مِنْهَا» (۲) أَخْرَجَهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَابْنُ حِبَّانَ وَالطَّبَرَانِيُّ وَغَيْرُهُمْ. (۲) قَوْلُهُ: عَلَى أَحَدِ حَاجِبَيْهِ؛ أَيْ مُحَاذِيًا لِحَاجِبِهِ الْأَيْمَنِ أَوِ الْأَيْسَرِ، هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، أَخْرَجَهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالطَّبَرَانِيُّ. (۳) قَوْلُهُ: وَلَا تُوضَعُ؛ أَيْ لَا تُلْقَى السُّتْرَةُ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ بَلْ تُغْرَزُ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ لَا يَحْصُلُ بِهِ، وَكَذَا لَا يَحْصُلُ بِالْخَطِّ فِي الْأَرْضِ، وَهَذَا هُوَ قَوْلُ أَكْثَرِ أَصْحَابِنَا. وَرُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُمَا اللهُ بِكَفَايَةِ الْوَضْعِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنِ الْغَرْزُ وَالْخَطِّ إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدْ سُتْرَةً كَالْمِحْرَابِ؛ لِحَدِيثِ: «فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَصاً فَلْيَخُطَّ خَطاً» (۳) أَخْرَجَهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَابْنُ مَاجَةَ، وَفِي سَنَدِهِ ضَعْفٌ غَيْرِ مَانِعٍ؛ لِجَوَازِ الْعَمَلِ بِهِ فِي الْفَضَائِلِ، قَالَ ابْنُ الْهُمَامِ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ: «السُّنَّةُ أَوْلَى بِالِاتِّبَاعِ». [٤] قَوْلُهُ: وَيَدْرَأُهُ؛ مِنَ الدَّرْءِ بِالْفَتْحِ بِمَعْنَى الدَّفْعِ أَيْ يَدْفَعُ الْمُصَلِّي الْمَارَّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ سُتْرَةٌ أَوْ كَانَتْ وَمَرَّ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ السُّتْرَةِ؛ لِقَوْلِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِذَا كَانَ أَحَدُكُمْ يُصَلِّي فَلَا يَدَعُ أَحَدًا يَمُرُّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ، وَلْيَدْرَأْ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ» (٥) أَخْرَجَهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ وَمُسْلِمٌ ... (ثم باقي الفقرة) بِالتَّسْبِيحِ أَوِ الْإِشَارَةِ لَا بِهِمَا إِنْ عَدِمَ سُتْرَةً، أَوْ مَرَّ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُمَا، وَكَفَى سُتْرَةُ الْإِمَامِ، وَجَازَ تَرْكُهَا عِنْدَ عَدَمِ الْمُرُورِ وَالطَّرِيقِ. [1] قَوْلُهُ: بِالتَّسْبِيحِ؛ أَيْ هُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ بَيْنَ دَفْعِهِ بِقَوْلِ: سُبْحَانَ اللهِ، وَبِالْإِشَارَةِ بِالْيَدِ أَوِ الرَّأْسِ أَوِ الْعَيْنِ، وَكَذَا بِالْجَهْرِ فَوْقَ الْجَهْرِ الْمُعْتَادِ فِي الْجَهْرِيَّةِ، وَبِالْجَهْرِ بِقِرَاءَةٍ فِي السِّرِّيَّةِ، وَهَذَا لِلرِّجَالِ، وَهُوَ مُسْتَفَادٌ مِنْ إِطْلَاقِ الْحَدِيثِ الْمَذْكُورِ، وَوَرَدَ فِي السُّنَنِ وَغَيْرِهَا: «إِذَا نَابَ أَحَدَكُمْ نَائِبَةٌ فَلْيُسَبِّحْ». وَلِلنِّسَاءِ مِنَ التَّصْفِيقِ؛ لِقَوْلِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّمَا التَّصْفِيقُ لِلنِّسَاءِ» (٢) أَخْرَجَهُ الشَّيْخَانِ وَغَيْرُهُمَا، وَهُوَ أَنْ تَضْرِبَ بِظَهْرِ أَصَابِعِ الْيُمْنَى أَوْ بِبَطْنِهَا عَلَى بَطْنِ كَفِّ الْيُسْرَى، أَوْ ظَهْرِهَا، فَلَوْ صَفَّقَ الرَّجُلُ أَوْ سَبَّحَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ لَمْ تَفْسُدِ الصَّلَاةُ، وَقَدْ تَرَكَا السُّنَّةَ. كَذَا فِي «التَّتَارْخَانِيَّةِ»، وَ«الْبِنَايَةِ»، وَ«الْبَحْرِ»، وَغَيْرِهَا. (٢) قَوْلُهُ: لَا بِهِمَا؛ أَيْ لَا يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَ التَّسْبِيحِ وَالْإِشَارَةِ؛ لِأَنَّ بِأَحَدِهِمَا كِفَايَةٌ، فَيُكْرَهُ مَا زَادَ عَلَى الْحَاجَةِ. [3] قَوْلُهُ: أَوْ مَرَّ بَيْنَهُ ... إِلَخْ؛ أَيْ مَرَّ الْمَارُّ بَيْنَ الْمُصَلِّي وَبَيْنَ السُّتْرَةِ عِنْدَ وُجُودِهَا. [٤] قَوْلُهُ: وَكَفَى سُتْرَةُ الْإِمَامِ؛ أَيْ لِلْمُقْتَدِينَ، فَإِنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ صَلَّى بِبَطْحَاءِ مَكَّةَ إِلَى سُتْرَةٍ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْقَوْمِ سُتْرَةٌ، كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى عَلَى مَنْ نَظَرَ صَحِيحَ الْبُخَارِيِّ وَمُسْلِمٍ. [0] قَوْلُهُ: وَجَازَ تَرْكُهَا؛ أَيْ لَوْ صَلَّى فِي مَكَانٍ لَا يَمُرُّ فِيهِ أَحَدٌ وَلَمْ يُوَاجِهِ الطَّرِيقَ لَا يَضُرُّ.
His closeness to one of his eyebrows, and it is not placed, nor is a line drawn, and he repels it (the passerby) because of the narration that he prayed towards a spear, recorded by Bukhari and others. Its length is a cubit and thickness of a finger. [1] His saying: 'by his closeness' is attached to the planting (gharz), due to the hadith: 'When one of you prays towards a sutrah, let him be close to it' recorded by Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, Tabarani and others. (2) His saying: 'on one of his eyebrows' meaning aligned with his right or left eyebrow, as transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, recorded by Abu Dawud and Tabarani. (3) His saying: 'and it is not placed' means the sutrah should not be thrown on the ground but planted, because the purpose is not achieved by placing it, and similarly a line on the ground does not achieve it. This is the saying of most of our companions. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that placing suffices if planting is not possible, and a line if no sutrah is found like a mihrab, due to the hadith: 'If there is no stick, let him draw a line' recorded by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah. Its chain has weakness but it is not an obstacle because acting upon it in virtues is permissible. Ibn al-Humam said: 'The sunnah is worthier of being followed.' [4] His saying: 'and he repels it' from 'dar' with fatha meaning to push, i.e., the one praying pushes the one passing in front of him if he has no sutrah or if he has one and the passer passes between him and the sutrah, due to his saying: 'When one of you prays, he should not let anyone pass in front of him, and let him repel as much as he can' recorded by Bukhari and Muslim. ... then the rest of the paragraph: By tasbih or gesture, not both, if he lacks a sutrah, or if a passer passes between him and it, and the imam's sutrah suffices, and it is permissible to omit it when there is no passing and no road. [1] His saying: 'by tasbih' means he has a choice between repelling him by saying 'Subhanallah' or by gesture with hand, head, or eye, likewise by raising voice above normal in loud prayers, and by raising voice in recitation in silent prayers. This is for men, derived from the absolute wording of the mentioned hadith. And it is narrated in the Sunan etc.: 'When something happens to one of you, let him say subhanallah.' For women it is by clapping, due to his saying: 'Clapping is only for women' recorded by the two Shaykhs and others. It is that she strikes with the back of the fingers of her right hand or its palm on the palm of her left hand or its back. If a man claps or a woman says subhanallah, the prayer is not invalidated but they have abandoned the sunnah. So recorded in al-Tatarakhaniyya, al-Binaya, al-Bahr, etc. (2) His saying: 'not both' means he should not combine tasbih and gesture because one is sufficient; it is disliked to increase above need. [3] His saying: 'or passes between him ...' means the passer passed between the worshipper and the sutrah when it exists. [4] His saying: 'and the imam's sutrah suffices' for the followers, for the Prophet prayed at the level ground of Mecca towards a sutrah and the people had no sutrah, as is not hidden from one who looks at Sahih Bukhari and Muslim. [0] His saying: 'and it is permissible to omit it' means if he prays in a place where no one passes and he does not face the road, it does not harm.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqaya regarding the sutrah (screen) in prayer. It begins by stating the recommended placement of the sutrah: close to the worshipper, aligned with one of his eyebrows. The sutrah should be planted (gharz) rather than laid on the ground, following the practice of the Prophet. Most Hanafis hold that a line drawn on the ground is insufficient, though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow it when no sutrah is available, citing a weak hadith. The commentator, citing Ibn al-Humam, prefers the stronger sunnah (planting). The passage then discusses the ruling on repelling someone who passes in front of a praying person: the worshipper may gently repel him, though this is recommended (ibaha/rulersa) rather than obligatory. The method of repelling differs by gender: men may say 'Subhanallah' or gesture subtly; women clap. Combining both tasbih and gesture is disliked. The imam's sutrah suffices for his followers, based on the Prophet's practice at Batha' Mecca. Finally, the sutrah may be omitted if no one is passing and the worshipper does not face a road. The passage illustrates the Hanafi approach of combining primary texts (hadith) with reasoned preference (istihsan) and gives the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) as the majority view.

Key Terms
سُتْرَة (sutrah): A physical barrier placed in front of the praying person to prevent people from passing directly in front of him.
يَدْرَأُ (yadra'u): To repel or push gently. It refers to the action of the praying person to prevent someone from passing in front of him during prayer.
تَصْفِيق (tasfiq): Clapping by striking the back of the right hand's fingers onto the palm of the left hand. This is the prescribed manner for women to alert the imam to a mistake in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a woman who says 'Subhanallah' instead of clapping to alert the imam during prayer?
A) Her prayer is invalid because she used the wrong method.
B) Her prayer is valid but she has left the sunnah.
C) She must repeat the prayer.
D) She should combine both clapping and tasbih.

Key Takeaway
The sutrah is a sunnah muakkadah; planting it is preferred, and repelling a passerby is done by tasbih for men and clapping for women without invalidating the prayer.

Repelling Disturbance in Prayer and Sutra Rulings
Ruling on repelling disturbance in prayer with tasbih/gesture and rules of sutra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling disturbance in prayer (tasbih vs gesture) and explain the conditions for sutra.

Core Idea
A worshiper may repel a disturbance in prayer by tasbih or gesture, but not both; sutra is sunnah, not obligatory.

In this passage, we learn that when something troublesome occurs during prayer—such as someone passing in front—the worshiper may respond in a limited way. The Sharh clarifies that the command to repel is a concession, not an obligation, and that the imam's sutra suffices for followers. We will unpack the evidence and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the permissible responses
The act is repelling a disturbance during prayer. Permissible responses: tasbih (saying SubhanAllah) for men, clapping for women, and gesturing with hand/head/eye for any worshiper. Also, raising voice in loud prayer or reciting aloud in quiet prayer are permissible.
These are actions to alert or repel, not to continue the prayer normally.
2
Analyze the ruling: permission vs obligation
The command in the hadith 'فليسبح' is interpreted as permissive (ibaha) not obligatory. The text says 'على سبيل الإباحة والرخصة لا على سبيل الوجوب' (on basis of permission and concession, not obligation).
This is a key Hanafi principle: imperative in context of prayer is not necessarily wajib; it may be ibaha.
3
Examine the sutra ruling
Sutra is recommended but not obligatory. The imam's sutra suffices for followers. If no one passes, it is permissible to pray without a sutra, though taking one is better.
Proof: The Prophet prayed with a sutra while his followers had none.
4
Combine the rulings: not both
The text states 'لا بهما' meaning do not combine tasbih and gesture. One is sufficient; combining is disliked (makruh).
Reason: needless excess beyond the need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالتسبيح أو الإشارة لا بهما إن عدم سترة، أو مر بينه وبينهما، وكفى سترة الإمام، وجاز تركها عند عدم المرور والطريق. وغيرهما، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة، والأمر بالدفع على سبيل الإباحة والرخصة لا على سبيل الوجوب. قوله : بالتسبيح ; أي هو مخير بين دفعه بقول : سبحان الله ، وبالإشارة باليد أو الرأس أو العين، وكذا بالجهر فوق الجهر المعتاد في الجهرية، وبالجهر بقراءة في السرية ، وهذا للرجال، وهو مستفاد من إطلاق الحديث المذكور، وورد في السنن وغيرها : «إذا ناب أحدكم نائبة فليسبح). وللنساء من التصفيق ; لقوله : «إنما التصفيق للنساء» (٢)، أخرجه الشيخان سن (1) وغيرهما وهو أن تضرب بظهر أصابع اليمني أو ببطنها على بطن كف اليسرى ، أو ظهرها، فلو صفّق الرجل أو سبحت المرأة لم تفسد الصلاة، وقد تركا السنة. كذا في «التاتارخانية»، و«البناية»، و«البحر»، وغيرها. قوله : لا بهما ; أي لا يجمع بين التسبيح والإشارة ; لأن بأحدهما كفاية، فيكره ما زاد على الحاجة. قوله : أو مر بينه ...الخ ; أي مرَّ المار بين المصلي وبين السترة عند وجودها. قوله : وكفى سترة الإمام ; أي للمقتدين، فإنّ النبي صلى ببطحاء مكة إلى سترة ولم يكن للقوم سترة ) ، كما لا يخفى على من نظر صحيح البخاري» و«مسلم». قوله : وجاز تركها ; أي لو صلّى في مكان لا يمر فيه أحد ولم يواجه الطريق لا يكره تركها; لعدم الاحتياج إليها، ومع ذلك الأولى اتخاذها. كذا في «الحلبة شرح المنية».
By tasbih or gesture, not both, if there is no sutra, or if someone passes between him and his sutra, and the sutra of the imam suffices, and it is permissible to leave it when there is no passing and no road. And others, and in this chapter there are many narrations, and the command to repel is on the basis of permission and concession, not on the basis of obligation. His saying: 'By tasbih' means he is given a choice between repelling it by saying 'SubhanAllah', and by gesturing with the hand, head, or eye, and likewise by raising the voice above the usual volume in loud prayers, and by reciting out loud in quiet prayers, and this applies to men, and it is derived from the general application of the mentioned hadith, and in the Sunan and others it is narrated: 'When something troublesome befalls one of you, let him say SubhanAllah.' And for women, clapping, because of his saying: 'Clapping is only for women' (2), narrated by the two Shaykhs and others, and it is that she strikes the back of the fingers of the right hand or its palm on the palm of the left hand or its back. If a man claps or a woman says SubhanAllah, the prayer is not invalidated, but they have abandoned the sunnah. So in al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Binaya, al-Bahr, and others. His saying: 'Not both' means he should not combine tasbih and gesture, because one is sufficient, so anything beyond need is disliked. His saying: 'or if someone passes between him...' etc. means the passer-by passed between the worshiper and the sutra when it is present. His saying: 'And the sutra of the imam suffices' means for the followers, because the Prophet (PBUH) prayed in the plain of Mecca towards a sutra while the people had no sutra, as is not hidden from one who looks at Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim. His saying: 'And it is permissible to leave it' means if he prays in a place where no one passes and does not face the road, it is not disliked to leave it, because there is no need for it, yet it is better to take it. So in al-Halba Sharh al-Munya.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that during prayer, if something occurs that requires attention (like someone passing), the worshiper may repel it by saying SubhanAllah (tasbih) or by making a gesture with the hand, head, or eyes, but not both. Women are to clap instead. The command to repel is not obligatory but a concession (ibaha). The author also discusses sutra: the imam's sutra suffices for the followers, and if one prays in a place where no one passes, it is permissible to omit the sutra, though taking it is still better. The evidence includes hadith from the Sunan and the two Sahihs.

Key Terms
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Saying 'SubhanAllah' during prayer to repel a disturbance
السترة (al-sutra): An object placed in front of the worshiper to prevent someone passing directly before him
الدفع (al-daf'): Repelling a nuisance or passer-by during prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a man do if someone passes in front of him during prayer?
A) Say SubhanAllah and gesture simultaneously
B) Either say SubhanAllah or gesture, not both
C) Clap to alert the passer
D) Continue prayer without any action

Key Takeaway
During prayer, repelling a disturbance is permissible via tasbih (men) or clap (women) or gesture, but one action suffices; sutra is recommended but not required when no one passes.

Classification of Makruh: Tahrimi and Tanzihi, and Ruling on Sadl al-Thawb
Definition and classification of makruh, applied to sadl al-thawb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling for sadl al-thawb during prayer.

Core Idea
Makruh in Hanafi law splits into tahrimi (sinful) and tanzihi (better avoided); sadl al-thawb is makruh tahrimi.

The Hanafi madhhab distinguishes two levels of disliked actions (makruh): one that is prohibitively disliked (tahrimi) and one that is lightly disliked (tanzihi). This lesson unpacks that distinction, explains how to identify each type from the evidence, and applies it to the specific case of letting one's garment hang loose during prayer (sadl al-thawb). Mastering this classification is essential for correctly grading actions that fall below haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Extract from the passage the definitions of makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi. Note that tahrimi is proven by a zanni (non-definitive) prohibition, while tanzihi is merely leaving the better.
The passage cites al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Halba for these definitions.
2
Understand the evidentiary criterion
The text states that when a ruling is called 'makruh' without qualification, one must look at its evidence. If there is a zanni prohibition (nahy zanni), it is tahrimi unless there is a divergent indicator. If there is no prohibition, only a suggestion to leave, it is tanzihi.
This is the key operational rule for classifying any given makruh.
3
Apply to sadl al-thawb
The passage brings the hadith: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade sadl in prayer...' This is a clear prohibition (nahy) from a hadith that is zanni al-thubut (not mutawatir). Therefore the ruling is makruh tahrimi.
The hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud, al-Hakim, and authenticated by Ibn Hibban and al-Tirmidhi.
4
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
Some later Hanafi scholars considered it tanzihi, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in al-Durr al-Mukhtar is tahrimi. Also, other madhahib may treat this differently.
Shafi'i school often equates makruh tahrimi with haram, but Hanafi maintains a distinct category.

And it is disliked: sadl al-thawb. He said in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 'The disliked in this chapter is of two types: one: that which is disliked prohibitively (makruh tahrimi), and that is the intended meaning when they use it unrestrictedly, as in al-Fath, and it is in the rank of wajib; it is only established by that by which the wajib is established, meaning by a prohibition that is zanni in transmission or indication. The second: the disliked in the sense of tanzih, and its referent is leaving what is better, and they often use it unrestrictedly as mentioned in al-Halba. So when they mention something as disliked, one must look at the evidence: if it is a zanni prohibition, it is judged as makruh tahrimi unless there is something that diverts the prohibition from indicating tahrim to indicating recommendation; if it is not a prohibition, but rather indicates leaving for a non-definitive reason, then it is tanzihi.' And al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munya and others mentioned that it is also known by a specific prohibition evidence that implies leaving a wajib or sunnah, so it becomes makruh tahrimi or tanzihi, and the tanzihi vary in severity and closeness to tahrimi according to the strength of the sunnah, for the levels of recommendation are diverse, like the levels of sunnah, wajib, and fard, and so are their opposites. His saying: sadl al-thawb: it is makruh tahrimi as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, because a prohibition has come concerning it. From Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him): 'The Messenger of Allah (PBUH) forbade sadl in prayer and that a man cover his mouth in prayer.' Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi fiqh commentary explains the two categories of disliked (makruh) actions in prayer: makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked). Makruh tahrimi is that which is proven by a zanni prohibition (a hadith that is not mutawatir) and is close to haram; it is in the rank of wajib in terms of the strength of evidence required. Makruh tanzihi is merely leaving the better, without a definitive prohibition. The commentator then applies this to the specific case of sadl al-thawb (letting one's garment hang loose during prayer), ruling it to be makruh tahrimi due to the explicit prohibition in the hadith of Abu Hurairah. The passage also clarifies that the severity of tanzihi can vary depending on how strongly the sunnah is emphasized.

Key Terms
سدل الثوب (sadl al-thawb): Allowing one's garment to hang loose without folding or adjusting it during prayer
المكروه تحريماً (al-makruh tahriman): An action that is prohibited by a zanni evidence; it is sinful to perform but does not reach the level of haram
المكروه تنزيهاً (al-makruh tanzihan): An action that is better to leave but not sinful; it is merely contrary to the preferred practice

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Sadl al-thawb during prayer is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school, proven by a clear but zanni hadith.

Ruling and Definition of Sadl al-Thawb in Prayer
Fiqh ruling with proof and lexical definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadl al-thawb in prayer, distinguish between makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi, and identify the definition of sadl according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sadl al-thawb in prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to an explicit prophetic prohibition.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on a specific posture in prayer: letting the garment hang loosely (sadl). The source passage not only states the ruling but also clarifies the two types of karahah (dislike) in Hanafi fiqh and provides lexical definitions. Understanding these distinctions is key to applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Ruling and Its Evidence
Identify the explicit statement that sadl is makruh tahrimi and the hadith cited as proof.
The hadith is a zanni dalil, so the ruling is makruh tahrimi, not haram.
2
Understand the Two Types of Karahah
Analyze the distinction between makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and makruh tanzihi (disliked as leaving the better).
Makruh tahrimi is established by a zanni prohibition; otherwise it is tanzihi.
3
Define Sadl Lexically and Technically
Examine the two definitions: (1) letting the garment hang without joining sides, (2) placing it on the head and shoulders and letting ends hang.
Both definitions ultimately refer to the same action, but they vary based on the garment type.
4
Apply the Definition to Specific Garments
The ruling applies specifically to garments like the taylasan (cloak) or handkerchief, not to all clothing.
For a qaba (long coat), sadl means throwing it over the shoulders without putting arms into sleeves.
5
Conclude with Practical Guidance
Determine how a Hanafi worshipper should avoid sadl in prayer by properly arranging the garment.
The mufta bihi ruling is makruh tahrimi, so one must avoid it and is excused only for necessity.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that 'sadl al-thawb' (letting down or hanging the garment loosely) is disliked in prayer. The commentator begins by clarifying the types of 'makruh' in Hanafi fiqh. According to al-Bahr al-Raiq, makruh is of two categories: makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked, which has the same legal weight as wajib in that it is established by a zanni proof) and makruh tanzihi (disliked as leaving the better, which is less severe). The commentator emphasizes that when scholars simply say 'makruh', one must examine the evidence: if there is a zanni prohibition, it is tahrimi unless there is a factor diverting it to recommendation; if there is no prohibition but simply a preference to leave, it is tanzihi. Al-Halabi adds that makruh can also be identified by the act itself: if it entails leaving an obligatory or sunnah act, then its karahah corresponds accordingly, and tanzihi varies in severity. The passage then states that sadl al-thawb is specifically makruh tahrimi as per al-Durr al-Mukhtar, citing the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited both sadl and covering the mouth in prayer. This hadith is recorded by Abu Dawud, al-Hakim, Ibn Hibban, and al-Tirmidhi. Next, the commentator explains the lexical definition of 'sadl' from al-Mughrib, which is a linguistic work by al-Mutrizi. The basic definition is to let a garment hang loosely without joining its sides. Another definition from al-Hidayah adds the element of placing the garment on the head and shoulders. The commentator reconciles these definitions, noting they ultimately refer to the same action. He further clarifies that these definitions apply specifically to garments like the taylasan (a type of cloak) or a handkerchief, not to all clothing. For a 'qaba' (a long coat), sadl means to throw it over the shoulders without putting the arms in the sleeves. The commentator also references Ibn al-Humam's point that even a handkerchief hanging from the shoulders should be properly placed during prayer. Thus, the ruling is clear: sadl in prayer is prohibitively disliked, and the definition depends on the type of garment.

Key Terms
السدل (al-sadl): To let a garment hang loosely without joining its sides, or to place it on the head and shoulders and let its ends hang. Specific to garments like the taylasan.
المكروه تحريماً (al-makruh tahrimi): An action that is prohibitively disliked, established by a zanni prohibition, and has the same legal weight as wajib in terms of its evidence.
الطيلسان (al-taylasan): A type of cloak that is worn over the shoulders, often without sleeves, and is customarily placed on the head and allowed to hang.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sadl al-thawb in prayer is makruh tahrimi due to a clear prophetic prohibition; understanding the types of karahah is essential for correct application.

Disliked Actions in Prayer: Sadl, Kaf, Abath, and ‘Aqs
Commentary defining and proving disliked actions in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sadl, kaf, abath, and ‘aqs in prayer, and identify the hadith proofs that support these rulings.

Core Idea
Four actions make prayer deficient: letting down the garment, folding it, fidgeting, and plaiting hair—all are prohibitively disliked.

The Hanafi school emphasizes khushu' (humility) in prayer. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya defines and proves four disliked actions that detract from this tranquility. Understanding these rulings helps the believer perfect his prayer and avoid what is makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions and their definitions
Read the Arabic definitions of sadl, kaf, abath, and ‘aqs as given in the commentary. Note that sadl has two interpretations, and kaf involves folding the garment or hair.
2
Locate the hadith proofs for kaf and abath
Find the two hadiths cited: (1) 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven limbs and not to fold hair or garment' for kaf. (2) 'Be still in prayer' for abath, and the weaker hadith about three disliked things.
The hadith for kaf is from the six authentic books; the hadith for abath is from Muslim.
3
Understand the Hanafi derivation of karahah tahrimiyyah
The negative command (nahy) in the hadith for kaf and the command for stillness imply prohibition. In Hanafi usul, nahy indicates karahah tahrimiyyah unless evidence shows it is haram.
Thus, these actions are prohibited but not at the level of haram.
4
Distinguish between light and excessive abath
Light fidgeting (with a worldly purpose but not need) is makruh tahrimi. If the movement becomes excessive (amal kathir), it invalidates the prayer. Note the exception: actions done for a genuine need, like scratching to relieve pain, are not disliked.
5
Note the ruling for ‘aqs and exceptions
Plaiting hair during prayer is also makruh, based on a narration that the Prophet forbade a man from praying with plaited hair. The common thread is actions that contradict the commanded stillness.

Book of Prayer: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. [2] 193 He lets it down without folding its sides, and it is said: He throws it over his head and lets it down over his shoulders. I say: This is concerning the taylasan (cloak). As for the qaba' (robe) and the like, he throws it over his shoulders without inserting his hands into its sleeves, and he folds its ends. [Biographical note about al-Mutarrizi] ... [1] His saying: 'He lets it down' means letting down, i.e., sadl, which is with a fatha on the sin and sukun on the dal, and it is also said with a fatha on the dal: he throws his garment like a cloak and the like without folding its sides. [2] His saying: 'And it is said': This is what was mentioned in al-Hidayah in his saying: 'He places his garment on his head and shoulders and lets down its ends from its sides.' Ibn al-Humam said in al-Fath: 'It applies to a handkerchief let down from his shoulders as many are accustomed, so it is necessary for one who has a handkerchief around his neck to put it down during prayer.' End. This interpretation and the previous one lead to the same result. [3] His saying: 'I say... etc.' indicates that the two mentioned interpretations do not include all garments; rather they are specific to the taylasan—which is a cloak—for throwing over the head, letting down on the shoulders, and releasing from the sides is customary only for the cloak and the like, such as a handkerchief. [4] His saying: 'He throws it'—He said in al-Ghunya: sadl is letting down without wearing, because sadl linguistically means letting down and releasing, and it must be qualified by not wearing, necessarily, because letting down the tail of a shirt and the like is not called sadl. [PAGE_194] 194 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. [1] And his folding (garment), and his fidgeting with it and his body, and his plaiting his hair. (And his folding) meaning he gathers its ends to protect from dust and the like. (And his fidgeting with it and his body, and his plaiting his hair.) [1] His saying: 'His folding'—with a fatha on the kaf and tashdid on the fa—meaning raising it when bending to prostration from in front of him or behind him. Al-Khayr al-Ramli analyzed that the karaah (dislike) in this is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The basis for this is the hadith: 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven limbs and not to fold hair or garment.' This also includes the dislike of the one praying having his sleeves rolled up. The mentioned hadith was narrated by the six (authentic books). This is in al-Fath. [2] His saying: 'And his fidgeting': al-abaht (fidgeting) is an action that has a purpose but not a religious one; what has no purpose is frivolity. This is in al-'Inaya, and the karaah is tahrimi as stated in al-Bahr. This applies when it is not excessive action; if it is excessive, it invalidates. It is also conditioned by not being due to need, for if it is a need like scratching the body to relieve pain, it is not disliked. The basis for this is the hadith: 'Verily Allah has disliked for you three things: fidgeting in prayer, obscenity in fasting, and laughter in graveyards.' Al-Quda'i narrated it in Musnad al-Shihab with a weak chain. It is also supported by the hadith: 'Be still in prayer' narrated by Muslim in his Sahih and others. [3] His saying: 'And his plaiting his hair': as narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade a man praying while his hair is plaited.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya is a commentary expanding on the matn's list of disliked actions in prayer. The author, a Hanafi faqih, discusses four specific actions: sadl (letting down a garment), kaf (folding the garment or hair), abath (fidgeting), and aqs (plaiting hair). For each, he provides definitions, distinguishes between types of garments, and gives proofs from hadith.

1. Sadl (السدل): The commentator first defines sadl as releasing or letting down a garment without folding its sides, offering two interpretations: (a) releasing without gathering sides, and (b) throwing it over the head and shoulders. He notes that these apply specifically to the taylasan (a cloak) or similar outer garments like a handkerchief; for a qaba' (robe), sadl means throwing it over shoulders without inserting arms into sleeves. Quoting al-Ghunya, he emphasizes that sadl requires the garment not to be worn in the normal manner; merely letting down the tail of a shirt is not sadl. The ruling for such a posture in prayer is disliked (makruh) according to the Hanafi school.

2. Kaf (الكف): This refers to folding or gathering parts of the garment or hair during prayer, such as raising the garment when going into prostration to avoid dust. The commentator states that al-Khayr al-Ramli considered this karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked). The proof is the hadith in which the Prophet (PBUH) said, 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven limbs and not to fold hair or garment.' This hadith is from the six canonical works (al-sittah) and indicates the prohibition of such actions. The commentator adds that rolling up sleeves also falls under this dislike.

3. Abath (العبث): This means fidgeting or playing with the body or clothing without a valid religious purpose. The commentator clarifies that if the action serves a legitimate need, such as scratching to relieve pain, it is not disliked. The karahah tahrimiyyah applies only to light, purposeless movements. If the action is excessive (amal kathir), it invalidates the prayer entirely. Two hadiths support this: a weaker narration from al-Quda'i stating Allah dislikes fidgeting in prayer, and the stronger hadith from Muslim commanding stillness in prayer. The commentator also distinguishes between actions with a worldly purpose (abath) and those with no purpose at all (safah); only the former is abath.

4. Aqs (عقص): This involves plaiting or tying the hair in a way that prevents it from spreading during prostration. The commentator refers to a narration forbidding a man from praying while his hair is plaited—this prevents full contact of the forehead with the ground? In the Hanafi school, this is also makruh.

Overall, the passage emphasizes that prayer requires humility and focus; any deviation from the standard posture or unnecessary movement detracts from this. The commentator uses authentic hadiths as evidence for the rulings and distinguishes between light actions (which are prohibited) and necessary ones (which are exempt). The authority_weight is based on Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted through the core Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
السدل (al-sadl): Letting down a garment without wearing it properly—i.e., placing it over the head/shoulders or releasing it without folding its sides, specifically for cloaks and similar outer garments.
الكف (al-kaf): Folding or gathering the garment or hair during prayer, such as raising the garment when going into prostration to avoid dust.
العبث (al-abath): Fidgeting or performing an action in prayer that has a worldly purpose but no religious benefit, provided it is not excessive.
العقص (al-'aqs): Plaiting or tying the hair such that it does not spread freely, specifically during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the ruling for 'fidgeting with the body' (العبث بالجسد) in prayer if it is not excessive and not for a need?
A) It is permissible (mubah) as long as it is light.
B) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
C) It is strictly forbidden (haram).
D) It invalidates prayer (mufsid).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any unnecessary action in prayer that contradicts tranquility is prohibitively disliked, and if excessive, invalidates the prayer.

Ruling of 'Aqs and Cracking Fingers in Prayer
Ruling with proof for two disliked actions in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for 'aqs before and during prayer and for cracking fingers, and explain the proof and the distinction between makruh tahrimi and mufsid.

Core Idea
A single action's ruling changes with timing: 'aqs before prayer is makruh tahrimi, during prayer it invalidates; cracking fingers is makruh tahrimi.

Have you ever wondered about seemingly small actions during prayer, like tying your hair or cracking your fingers? This lesson unpacks two specific rulings from the Hanafi school: gathering the hair ('aqs) and cracking the fingers. You will learn that these are not merely disliked but approach prohibition, and crucially, that the same action of 'aqs has different rulings depending on when it occurs. By understanding the proofs, you can apply these rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
First, identify what 'aqs and farqa'at al-asabi' mean. 'Aqs is gathering and tying hair on the head, similar to a bun. Cracking fingers is interlacing and pulling them to produce a sound.
The source quotes al-Mughrib for definitions.
2
Identify the timing distinction for 'aqs
Notice that the ruling for 'aqs depends on when it occurs. If done before entering prayer, the Hanafi ruling is makruh tahrimi. If done during prayer, it invalidates the prayer (mufsid). This is a key point: the same act changes legal consequence based on timing.
The text says 'all this applies if 'aqs was before prayer; as for 'aqs during prayer, it invalidates.'
3
Analyze the proofs for cracking fingers
Examine the hadith cited: 'Do not crack your fingers while you are in prayer.' Though transmitted with a weak chain, it is supported by other narrations. Understand how the Hanafi school derives the ruling of makruh tahrimi from a prohibition (la taf'al).
The dalil_block indicates the hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Evaluate the dispute with al-Nawawi
Al-Nawawi (Shafi'i) considered these actions makruh tanzihi. The Hanafi text, citing Halbat al-Mujalli and al-Binaya, prefers tahrimi. Understand the basis: the context of the hadiths and the stronger implication of prohibition.
This is a cross-madhhab ikhtilaf. The Hanafi tarjih authority here is the later commentators.
5
Derive the mufta bihi position
Consolidate: the operative ruling for fatwa is that 'aqs before prayer and cracking fingers are makruh tahrimi; 'aqs during prayer invalidates. This is based on the preponderance of evidence and the preference of later Hanafi authorities.
The authority_weight is fatawa_mutakhkhirin.

في «المغرب» : هو جمع الشعر على الرأس ، وقيل : ليه وإدخال أطرافه في أصوله، وفرقعة أصابعه، وهو أن يغمرها ويمدها حتى تصوت معقوص، أخرجه عبد الرزاق في مصنفه، وأبو داود وابن ماجة، والترمذي، والطبراني، وإسحاق بن راهويه، وغيرهم.
الأشبه بسياق الأحاديث أن الكراهة تحريمية، قاله في «حلبة المجلي شرح منية المصلي» بعدما نقل عن النووي أنها كراهة تنزيهية، وهذا كله إذا كان العقص قبل الصلاة، وأما العقص في الصلاة فمفسد. كذا في «البناية». قوله : جمع الشعر؛ أي أن يتضفر به حول الرأس كعقد النساء، ويجمع شعره فيعقده في مؤخر رأسه، وقيل : أن يجمعه على وسط رأسه.
قوله : ليه؛ اللي بفتح اللام وتشديد الياء بالفارسية : يجيدن.
قوله : وفرقعة أصابعه؛ على وزن دحرجة، الأصل فيه حديث : «لا تفرقع أصابعك وأنت في الصلاة»، أخرجه ابن ماجة بسند ضعيف، وله شاهد في مسند أحمد ومعجم الطبراني وسنن الدارقطني.
وعن أبي سعيد المقبري : أنه رأى أبا رافع مولى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مر بحسن بن علي رضي الله عنهما وهو يصلي قائما، وقد غرز ضفره في قفاه فحلها أبو رافع فالتفت حسن إليه مغضبا، فقال أبو رافع : أقبل على صلاتك ولا تغضب فإني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : ذلك كفل الشيطان، يعني مقعد الشيطان يعني مغرر ضفره. في سنن أبي داود وسنن الترمذي وغيرها. وعن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : أنه رأى عبد الله بن الحارث ورأسه معقوص من ورائه فقام فجعل يحله فلما انصرف أقبل إلى ابن عباس فقال : ما لك ورأسي قال : إني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول إنما مثل الذي يصلي ورأسه معقوص مثل الذي يصلي وهو مكتوف. في سنن النسائي الكبرى والمجتبى وسنن أبي داود وغيرها. فعن علي رضي الله عنه قال : لا تفقع أصابعك وأنت في الصلاة. في سنن ابن ماجة ومسند البزار وغيرها. ورجال إسناده ثقات.
Book of Prayer: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it, and cracking his fingers. In 'al-Mughrib': It is gathering hair on the head, and it is said: twisting and inserting its ends into its roots. And cracking his fingers: it is to interlace them and pull them until they make a sound. 'Aqs (gathering hair) is reported by Abd al-Razzaq in his Musannaf, and Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Tabarani, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and others. The most apparent from the context of the hadiths is that the dislike is prohibitively disliked (tahrimi), stated in 'Halbat al-Mujalli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli' after quoting al-Nawawi that it is tanzihi (permissible dislike). And all this applies if the 'aqs was before prayer; as for 'aqs during prayer, it invalidates. Likewise in 'al-Binaya'. His statement: gathering hair: meaning to plait it around the head like the knot of women, and to gather his hair and tie it at the back of his head, and it is said: to gather it on the middle of his head. His statement: 'layh'; 'lay' with fatha on lam and tashdid on ya in Persian: to twist. His statement: and cracking his fingers: on the scale of dahrqah; its basis is the hadith: 'Do not crack your fingers while you are in prayer', reported by Ibn Majah with a weak chain, and it has a witness in Musnad Ahmad, Mu'jam al-Tabarani, and Sunan al-Daraqutni. And from Abu Sa'id al-Maqbari: that he saw Abu Rafi', the freed slave of the Prophet, pass by Hasan ibn Ali while he was praying standing, and he had plait his braid at his nape, and Abu Rafi' undid it, so Hasan turned to him angrily. Abu Rafi' said: 'Turn to your prayer and do not be angry, for I heard the Messenger of Allah say: That is the portion of the devil, meaning the sitting place of the devil, meaning the root of his braid.' In Sunan Abi Dawud, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, etc. And from Ibn Abbas: that he saw Abd Allah ibn al-Harith with his hair gathered behind him, so he stood and began to undo it. When he finished, Ibn al-Harith turned to Ibn Abbas and said: 'What is wrong with me and my head?' He said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: The likeness of one who prays with his hair gathered is like one who prays while he is tied up.' In Sunan al-Nasa'i al-Kubra, al-Mujtaba, Sunan Abi Dawud, etc. And from Ali: 'Do not crack your fingers while you are in prayer.' In Sunan Ibn Majah, Musnad al-Bazzar, etc. Its narrators are trustworthy.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the section on what is disliked in prayer. The author discusses two disliked actions: 'aqs (gathering the hair) and farqa'at al-asabi' (cracking the fingers). For 'aqs, the text first defines it as gathering hair on the head, specifically tying it like women's buns. The ruling depends on timing: if done before entering prayer, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike) according to the preferred view, contrary to al-Nawawi's opinion of tanzihi. If done during prayer, it actually invalidates the prayer (mufsid). This distinction is crucial: the same action has a different ruling based on when it occurs. For cracking fingers, the primary proof is the hadith 'Do not crack your fingers while you are in prayer,' though with a weak chain, supported by other narrations. The text also cites the incident with Hasan ibn Ali where Abu Rafi' undid his braid during prayer, and the Prophet's statement that such gathering is the 'portion of the devil.' The hadith comparing a praying person with gathered hair to one who is tied up reinforces the prohibition. The overall tone is that these are not merely disliked but approach prohibition.

Key Terms
العقص (al-'aqs): Gathering and tying the hair on the head, often at the back or crown, similar to women's buns.
فرقعة الأصابع (farqa'at al-asabi'): Cracking the fingers by interlocking and pulling them to produce a sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the ruling of gathering the hair ('aqs) during prayer?
A) It is makruh tanzihi
B) It is makruh tahrimi
C) It invalidates the prayer (mufsid)
D) It is permissible (mubah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'aqs before prayer (makruh tahrimi) and during prayer (mufsid), and considers cracking fingers makruh tahrimi.

Ruling of Turning and Moving Pebbles in Prayer
Explains the ruling of looking around and moving pebbles with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each type of turning in prayer and explain whether turning with the eyes, face, or chest affects validity.

Core Idea
Turning the chest in prayer invalidates; turning the face is makruh tahrimi; moving pebbles is makruh tahrimi unless needed.

In this lesson, we examine two common actions that may disturb prayer: looking around (iltifat) and fidgeting with the ground (qalb al-hasa). The text provides clear rulings based on prophetic warnings, classifying turning into three categories and emphasizing the severity of unnecessary movement. Understanding these distinctions helps the believer maintain khushu' and avoid sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage covers two actions: al-iltifat (turning) and qalb al-hasa (moving pebbles). For turning, the text first defines it and then classifies three types with different rulings. For moving pebbles, it states the default ruling and a condition.
Use the classification from al-Ghunya to distinguish the types.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith from Tirmidhi ('Beware of turning... it is destruction') and Bukhari ('a snatch from the devil') to establish the prohibition for iltifat. For moving pebbles, no specific hadith is quoted; rather, it is compared to the action of the people of Lut.
The hadith are ahad but considered strong enough for tahrim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'إياك' and the word 'هلكة' indicate a severe warning, which the Hanafi school interprets as proof of tahrim (prohibitive dislike) rather than mere tanzih (light dislike). The Bukhari hadith uses 'اختلاس' (snatching), further emphasizing the harm.
This is the key point of the dispute with other schools.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., al-Nawawi) consider turning with the face as makruh tanzihi. The text explicitly prefers tahrimi, citing al-Halba and al-Bahr.
The practical consequence is whether the action incurs sin.
5
Apply the condition for moving pebbles
Moving pebbles is makruh tahrimi, but the text adds a condition: if there is a need (e.g., hot ground), it becomes permissible. This is based on the principle of necessity.
The condition is found in al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Source Text

والتفاته، وقلب الحصى ليسجد
(والتفاته) وهو أن ينظر يمينا وشمالا مع لي عنقه، وأما النظر بمؤخر عينيه بلا لي العنق فلا يكره.
(وقلب الحصى ليسجد) وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة تحريمية كما في «الحلبة» و«البحر»، وذكر في «الغنية»: إنه مكروه خارج الصلاة أيضا؛ لأنه عمل قوم لوط صلى الله على نبينا وعليه وسلم، وهو مقيد بعدم الحاجة كإراحة الأصابع، كما في «الدر المختار» وحواشيه.
قوله : والتفاته؛ لما روى الترمذي مرفوعا: إياك والالتفات في الصلاة، فإن الالتفات في الصلاة هلكة، وفي «صحيح البخاري»: «هو اختلاس يختلسه الشيطان من صلاة العبد»، وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة فيه تحريمية. كذا في «البحر».
قوله : لي؛ بفتح اللام وتشديد الياء: أي صرفه عن جهة القبلة.
قوله : بمؤخر؛ بضم الميم وكسر الخاء المعجمة: طرف العين الذي يلي الصدغ.
قوله : فلا يكره؛ قال في «الغنية»: الالتفات على ثلاثة: التفات مفسد وهو بالصدر، والتفات مكروه وهو بالوجه، والتفات غير مكروه وهو بالعين بدون تحويل الوجه، لما روى الترمذي والنسائي وابن حبان وصححه عن ابن عباس «كان يلحظ يمينا وشمالا، ولا يلوي عنقه».
قوله : وقلب الحصى؛ بفتح الحاء المهملة، والصاد كذلك: سنكريزه، قال...
And his turning, and turning pebbles to prostrate. (His turning) is that he looks right and left while bending his neck, but looking with the corner of his eyes without bending the neck is not disliked. (And turning pebbles to prostrate) and it should be that the dislike is prohibitively disliked (tahrimi) as in 'al-Halba' and 'al-Bahr', and mentioned in 'al-Ghunya': it is disliked outside prayer as well, because it is the action of the people of Lut, peace be upon our Prophet and upon him, and it is restricted to when there is no need, like resting the fingers, as in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' and its glosses. His statement: and his turning; because al-Tirmidhi narrated in marfu' form: Beware of turning in prayer, for turning in prayer is destruction, and in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'It is a snatch that the devil snatches from the prayer of the servant', and it should be that the dislike is tahrimi. Likewise in 'al-Bahr'. His statement: 'lay'; with fatha on lam and tashdid on ya: meaning turning away from the direction of the qibla. His statement: 'bimu'akhkhir'; with damma on mim and kasr on kha' mu'jama: the corner of the eye that is next to the temple. His statement: so it is not disliked; He said in 'al-Ghunya': turning is of three types: turning that invalidates, which is with the chest; turning that is disliked, which is with the face; and turning that is not disliked, which is with the eyes without turning the face, because al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Hibban narrated and authenticated from Ibn Abbas: 'He would glance right and left and not turn his neck.' His statement: and turning pebbles; with fatha on ha' muhmala and likewise on sad: sang-rize, he said...
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning two disliked actions in prayer: al-iltifat (turning) and qalb al-hasa (moving pebbles). For turning, the text defines it as looking right and left with the neck turned. Looking with only the eyes without turning the neck is not disliked. The proof is the hadith 'Beware of turning in prayer, for turning in prayer is destruction' and the hadith in Bukhari that it is a snatch from the devil. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The text also cites al-Ghunya's classification: turning with the chest invalidates the prayer, turning with the face is disliked, and turning with the eyes alone is not disliked. For moving pebbles to prepare the place of prostration, the ruling is also makruh tahrimi, and it is disliked even outside prayer because it resembles the actions of the people of Lut. However, it is conditional on there being no need, such as when the ground is hot and one needs to cool the pebbles. The passage emphasizes that these actions are prohibited strongly, not merely discouraged.

Key Terms
الالتفات (al-iltifat): Turning the head right or left during prayer, specifically with the neck.
قلب الحصى (qalb al-hasa): Turning or smoothing pebbles or gravel on the ground to prepare for prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of turning in prayer invalidates the prayer?
A) Turning with the eyes
B) Turning with the face
C) Turning with the chest
D) Turning the neck slightly

Key Takeaway
Turning with the chest invalidates prayer; unnecessary turning with the face and moving pebbles are makruh tahrimi; slight eye movements are permissible.

The Ruling on Smoothing Pebbles Once in Prayer
Explanation of the exception for one motion to smooth pebbles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on smoothing pebbles in prayer and identify the hadith proof that permits one motion as a concession.

Core Idea
One smooth pebble is permitted; more is disliked — necessity allows the concession.

In salah, unnecessary motion is discouraged. Among such motions is smoothing the ground for prostration. This lesson examines the specific concession that permits one motion, based on the Prophet's ﷺ guidance to Ma'yiqib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is taswiyat al-hasa (smoothing pebbles) during prayer. By default, any smoothing is disliked (makruh) because it is unnecessary motion that may distract from khushu'.
The matn originally states that smoothing pebbles is disliked 'except once'.
2
Recognize the exception
The phrase 'except once' introduces a rukhsah (concession). This means that one motion is permitted when needed, though it is better to avoid it entirely.
The commentator clarifies this is a rukhsah, not the original ruling (azimah).
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Do not wipe the pebbles while you are praying, but if you must, then once.' This hadith is the primary dalil. The general command prohibits wiping, but the exception allows one motion out of necessity.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are two narrations within the Hanafi school: the more apparent one allows one motion; another considers even one motion disliked. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that one motion is permitted.
This is an example of tarjih (preference) within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
If a worshipper needs to smooth the ground once (e.g., to place the nose properly during sujood), it is permissible (mubah). More than one motion is makruh (disliked). Avoiding it entirely is preferable.
The ruling applies to any similar necessary motion in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : إلا مرة ؛ هذا رخصة ، فالأولى تركها إن أمكن، لما روى مسلم وغيره عن معيقيب : إن رسول الله ﷺ قال في الرجل يسوّي التراب حيث يسجد ، قال : «إن كنت فاعلاً فواحدة)، وأخرج أصحاب الكتب الستة مرفوعاً: «لا تمسح الحصى وأنت تُصلّي، فإن كنت لا بد فاعلاً فواحدة). وفي أظهر الروايتين أنه يسويه مرة.
He said: 'except once' – this is a concession, and it is better to leave it if possible, because Muslim and others narrated from Ma'yiqib that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said regarding a man smoothing the dirt where he prostrates: 'If you have to do it, then once.' And the authors of the six books narrated in marfu' form: 'Do not wipe the pebbles while you are praying, but if you must, then once.' And in the more apparent of the two narrations, he smooths it once.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on disliked actions in prayer. The original matn stated that smoothing pebbles is disliked except once. The commentator explains that this exception is a rukhsa (concession), meaning it is permitted but better to avoid altogether. The proof comes from two hadith: one from Ma'yiqib where the Prophet ﷺ allowed one motion if necessary, and another narrated in the six books prohibiting wiping pebbles except once. There is also an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: in the view of Imam Muhammad (according to the apparent narration), he may smooth it once; in another narration, even that is disliked. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one motion is permitted.

Key Terms
تسوية الحصى (taswiyat al-hasa): Smoothing the pebbles or earth on the ground to make it level for prostration.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession allowing an action that is normally prohibited or disliked due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on smoothing pebbles more than once during prayer?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
One motion to smooth pebbles in prayer is permitted as a rukhsah; more than one is makruh.

Ruling on Placing Hand on Waist in Prayer
Proof that placing hand on waist is disliked with tahrimi karahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing the hand on the waist during prayer and explain why it is classified as makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Placing the hand on the waist in prayer is prohibitively disliked because it contradicts khushu and is explicitly prohibited in hadith.

Why is a simple hand position during prayer a matter of serious discussion? In the Hanafi school, certain postures are not merely discouraged but are considered prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi). This lesson examines one such posture—placing the hand on the waist (al-takhasşur)—and unpacks the evidence that leads to this classification. You will learn not only the ruling but the reasoning behind its severity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
First, recognize the act under discussion: placing the hand on the waist during prayer. The commentator clearly states the ruling: it is disliked (makruh), and the apparent level is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The Arabic term 'تخصره' means putting the hand on the waist.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The prohibition has come in the 'five books' of Hadith (excluding Sunan Ibn Majah) as well as in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and others. Identify that the evidence is ahad hadith, not mutawatir.
The five books are the standard Sunan collections: Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i. Ibn Majah is excluded here.
3
Determine the Level of Karahah
The commentator states 'الظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية' – the apparent is that the dislike is tahrimi. He supports this by citing al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Understand why the level is tahrimi and not tanzihi.
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; it requires a strong prohibition from a zanni dalil.
4
Analyze the Thubut and Dalala
The hadith are ahad, so thubut is zanni. The prohibition is explicit, so dalala is clear but still zanni overall. A zanni dalil can create karahah tahrimi but not haram, which requires qat'i proof.
This explains why the action is not declared haram despite the explicit prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وتخصره: أي وضع اليد على الخاصرة، لورود النهي عن ذلك في الكتب الخمسة، سوى سنن ابن ماجه، ومصنف ابن أبي شيبة وغيرها، والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية، كما في البحر.
He said: 'And placing his hand on his waist': that is, placing the hand on the waist, because prohibition of that has come in the five books, except Sunan Ibn Majah, and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and others, and the apparent is that the dislikeness is tahrimi, as in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage addresses the disliked action of placing one hand on the waist (al-takhasşur) during prayer. The commentator clarifies that this action is makruh, and according to the apparent ruling, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it is contrary to humility and has been explicitly prohibited in many hadith collections. The refererence to 'the five books' signifies the standard hadith works excluding Ibn Majah. The commentator cites 'al-Bahr' (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) for the tahrimi classification.

Key Terms
الخاصرة (al-khaasirah): The waist area; placing the hand on the waist is a specific posture disliked during prayer.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an action that is close to haram due to a strong prohibition from a zanni dalil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the level of dislike (karahah) for placing the hand on the waist during prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) Makruh tanzihi
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Placing the hand on the waist during prayer is makruh tahrimi because the explicit prohibition in ahad hadith establishes a strong dislike but not absolute prohibition.

The Ruling on Stretching in Prayer
Ruling with proof on stretching in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on stretching in prayer, explain its basis in khushu' and the hadith, and apply the general principle that any action not beneficial for the prayer is disliked.

Core Idea
Stretching in prayer is makruh because it contradicts khushu' and indicates laziness.

This passage addresses a common but often overlooked action in prayer: stretching the body. The commentator explains that such movement is disliked because it undermines the humility (khushu') required in salah and reveals a lazy attitude. He then provides a general principle that helps us evaluate any extraneous movement during prayer: if it does not contribute to correcting or perfecting the prayer, it is makruh. This ruling is supported by the prophetic command to be still.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage defines 'al-tamatți' (stretching) and states that it is makruh (disliked).
The act is specifically stretching the body in a lazy manner.
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
Two reasons are given: (1) it is contrary to khushu' (humility), and (2) it indicates laziness.
Both reasons relate to the internal state of the worshiper.
3
Extract the general principle
The commentator states a general rule: every action in prayer that does not benefit the worshiper in correcting the prayer is disliked.
This principle can be applied to other movements.
4
Identify the dalil
The hadith 'اسكنوا في الصلاة' (Be still in prayer) from Sahih Muslim is cited as evidence.
The command implies stillness, so stretching violates that command.
5
Note the source of the principle
The commentator attributes this principle to al-'Ayni in al-Binayah, indicating its authority in the Hanafi school.
Al-'Ayni is a respected Hanafi jurist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وتَمَطَّيه: بفتح التاء والميم وكسر الطاء المشددة: وكراهته لكونه منافياً للخشوع، ومنبئاً عن التكاسل، وكل عمل في الصلاة ليس بمفيد للمصلي في إصلاح صلاته فهو مكروه، كما نص عليه العيني في البناية لحديث: «اسكنوا في الصلاة) أخرجه مسلم.
He said: 'And stretching himself': with fatha on the ta and mim and kasra on the shaddaed ta: its dislike is because it is contrary to humility and indicates laziness, and every action in prayer that is not beneficial for the worshiper in correcting his prayer is disliked, as al-'Ayni stated in al-Binayah based on the hadith: 'Be still in prayer' narrated by Muslim.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the disliked act of stretching (al-tamatți) during prayer. The commentator explains that stretching is makruh because it opposes khushu' (humility) and indicates laziness. He then provides a general principle: any action in prayer that does not directly help in perfecting the prayer is disliked. This principle is supported by the hadith 'Be still in prayer' narrated by Muslim, which commands stillness and prohibits unnecessary movements. The commentator cites al-'Ayni's al-Binayah as the source for this principle.

Key Terms
التمطي (al-tamatți): Stretching the body; extending the limbs in a manner indicating laziness.
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer; the heart and body being present and still.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the primary reason for the dislike of stretching in prayer?
A) It disturbs other worshippers
B) It is contrary to khushu'
C) It invalidates the prayer
D) It is a form of arrogance

Key Takeaway
Stretching in prayer is disliked because it lacks khushu', and any action not beneficial for the prayer is generally makruh, as supported by the hadith command to be still.
